  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5d390ed3-f869-4b9e-b860-981cad00975f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

There are lovers, friends and their children, school programs to attend. In the midst of all the ordinary happiness a vampire from Anita's past reaches out. She was supposed to be dead, killed in an explosion, but the Mother of All Darkness is the first vampire, their dark creator. It's hard to kill a god. This dark goddess has reached out to her here-in St. Louis, home of everyone Anita loves most. The Mother of All Darkness has decided she has to act now or never, to control Anita, and all the vampires in America. <br /><br /> The Mother of All Darkness believes that the triumvirate created by master vampire Jean-Claude with Anita and the werewolf Richard Zeeman has enough power for her to regain a body and to immigrate to the New World. But the body she wants to possess is already taken. Anita is about to learn a whole new meaning to sharing her body, one that has nothing to do with the bedroom. And if the Mother of All Darkness can't succeed in taking over Anita's body for herself, she means to see that no one else has the use of it, ever again. Even Belle Morte, not always a friend to Anita, has sent word: "Run if you can..."</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105169854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9975728410270501408">I am normally a loyal fan & have a lot of patience for LKH in general. I have hung in there with Anita (& Merry) & when many fans started turning away calling the series "porn" - I still liked it, still defended it, was still very into the stories & the characters (bar a few). <br/><br/>This book crashed & burned the series IMO. It was a pathetic mess. I don't even know what this was. I think LKH's massive amount of hubris made her lose the plot. <br/><br/>This was an extension of LKH's narcissistic ego (she even d</span>
  <span id="freeText9975728410270501408" style="display:none">I am normally a loyal fan &amp; have a lot of patience for LKH in general. I have hung in there with Anita (&amp; Merry) &amp; when many fans started turning away calling the series "porn" - I still liked it, still defended it, was still very into the stories &amp; the characters (bar a few). <br /><br />This book crashed &amp; burned the series IMO. It was a pathetic mess. I don't even know what this was. I think LKH's massive amount of hubris made her lose the plot. <br /><br />This was an extension of LKH's narcissistic ego (she even dressed Anita in clothing that SHE herself has posed in. Look at her gallery on her website...although it's not the 1st time she's done this). It makes me wonder - has being married to a younger man done more harm than good b'c her blogs often talk about nothing but the great sex she is getting from him &amp; clearly...CLEARLY she is projecting into her novels. This one more than ever. <br /><br />God I don't even know where to begin w/this book it was such a mess. Not even a hot mess...just a plain old pathetic, tired, overused mess.<br /><br />What she did in this book:<br /><br /> #1 - Anita's vagina has officially become the Macgyver of all vagina's. <br /><br />It can DO anything.....Next up - Anita gains another power &amp; cures cancer, AID's, smallpox, what have you - all while finally brokering peace between the Isreali's &amp; Palestinian's. What does the President have to say about it?? "If anyone can do it. Anita can!"<br /><br />Although IMO, her cooter more came across like a Venus Flycrotch. Once these men &amp; women have a taste, there's no getting out..muuuah ha ha!! <br /><br />No seriously - Um...she doesn't even have to raise the ardeur anymore to even roll people? All she has to do is have sex full stop? See what happens with Meph/Devil. See?? Venus Flycrotch. That shit is dangerous. <br /><br /><i>(Oh yeah, she does women now too but don't worry - she only kisses &amp; grinds the gal while getting done from behind. Greedy girl still saves the pole for herself). </i><br /><br /> #2 - LKH officially relegates the fabulous character of Jean Claude to nothing more than a mere prop to help Anita deal with her faux (&amp; I mean faux as in - cringe inducing it's so fake) angst. <br /><br />I'm not surprised this has been a long time coming. LKH is in love with her were's (esp. b'c Nate &amp; Micha seem to be an paper mosh up of her hubby) &amp; as a result - JC wasn't in the last THREE books! <br /><br />But what she did to him here?? Shocking. As my friend said - she turned him into a "pussy whipped fool" <br /><br />It also seems she is letting him go b'c apparently she no longer minds sharing him w/other women or men. <br /><br /> #3 - before the book was released LKH banged on &amp; on on her blog how she killed a character &amp; it was soooo upsetting for her &amp; we the reader will be "destroyed by it."<br /><br /> **SPOILER**<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Haven?? Seriously? Haven? I have to laugh in LKH's face &amp; spit out my water while doing it! She is so out of touch it's not funny. <br /><br />I mean for God's sake - we never even saw Anita sleep with him! And not like there is any emotional resonance to any of her sex scenes anymore - but that only compounds the reason for zero emotional connection!<br /><br />WTF Ms. Hamilton? WTF..??<br /><br /><br />#4 - Here's what's the funniest to me - she fishes in her work as to how people feel &amp; see her via her characters. <br /><br />Anita is like an emotional robot...."I don't understand why Haven would go for Nathaniel". And then JC has to lay it out in layman's terms &amp; Richard has to bare his soul. It is a joke b'c it's on such a personal level for LKH.<br /><br />LKH has NO sense of humor so she herself, doesn't "get" it...see things that other people would b'c they have a modicum of humility that a sense of humor affords a person. <br /><br />Therefore, Anita doesn't have one either &amp; we have this pathetic scene written in. This emotional fishing scene was more of LKH trying to justify her reasons for having Anita be a sex goddess who people can't help but get addicted to. It just so sad. LKH needs to separate herself &amp; get a grip on her ego.<br /><br />Wah, wah...LKH, seriously - if you need to be reassured by your characters b'c down deep you know that you are so insecure you're on the verge of a nervous breakdown - maybe you should rethink the younger man thing. <br /><br />Like I said, it's a joke b'c it's so obviously personal. I'm actually embarrassed for her. <br /><br /><br />#5 - She creepily has a 5 year old show his attraction to Anita. Yuck. Ick. So f-ing gross. I really don't know the point of this bit of info. <br /><br /><br />#6 - She doesn't explain (at all) Anita's apparent new power being able to steal other vampire powers.<br /><br /><br />#7 - The Sex Scenes. Come people! They're just NOT hot. LKH thinks she is writing progressive, great sex. <br /><br />For the 1st time I can say it was like actual bad, cheesy porn (I actually can't believe I am saying this)! What makes a sex scene hot &amp; great is the emotional connection you have to the characters. You care about them so care about what's happening to them.<br /><br />Tell me why I should care about Anita in an orgy/gang bang, getting it on w/characters I have never met before, in a room full of people who love her &amp; are forced to watch her seduce stranger after stranger? <br /><br />Or even better - partake with people they normally never would b'c they happen to be there when she unleashes the ardeur?<br /><br />Honestly - it's cringe inducing b'c Anita comes across as used up. She comes across whoreish for power &amp; just keeps using her sex to get more &amp; more of it. It's just gross. <br /><br /><br />#8 - LKH &amp; Anita's love of Nate. Ever since he came on the scene, Anita's boundaries have been seriously pushed... I mean pushed (Furry sex anyone)? <br /><br />She can't see the forest for the trees, she is fool for his shit. He is completely passive aggressive in his need for her to be Dominant. She goes out of her mind &amp; way for him to the detriment of other characters who are far more interesting.<br /><br />Haven - was actually truly interesting to me. And in so many ways - he wanted to be equal with her. What does LKH do? Kill him for it b'c Anita can't have any dominates in her life. She is after all the Queen Bee. <br /><br />So all these once great, complicated characters? JC, Richard, Haven, Auggie, Requiem, Wicked Truth, London (where is London BTW?).....<br /><br />They have been made shadows of themselves. Tweaked to fit in &amp; just accept whatever bullshit Anita throws at them. And if they don't? Watch out! That Macgyver punani may just smother them in their sleep. <br /><br />Laurell K Hamilton......it's time you got a grip &amp; got over yourself. Do whatever it is you have to do to get clear, get a sense of humor &amp; lighten up in order to gain some real perspective &amp; be truly creative.<br /><br />Lose the chip on your shoulder, it's doing nothing but hurting your creation &amp; making her laughing stock. You can stop proving things to all the people in your life who told you, you were crap &amp; your writing sucked. Your a success now &amp; a pioneer - we got it.<br /><br />Enough rebellion &amp; making points just b'c you've gotten to the stage in your career where you can. You are abusing your success &amp; laying your true talent to waste. Just write. <br /><br />People aren't jealous of Anita b'c she doesn't have the right looks to fit in with the other mother's or b'c she has a harem of gorgeous men.....you have actually made her highly unlikable b'c she is so out of touch with the reality of things.<br /><br />To put it straight - Anita is a total ass. Completely delusional, self-righteous, demanding, greedy, selfish, grumpy &amp; just not cool at all.<br /><br />Seriously...no amount of "creamy goodness" is that appealing. Yuk. <br /><br />Get a reality check finally so you can get the grip you so desperately need, then get a therapist in order to get clear so you can be the great storyteller we know you can be. <br /><br />If not - put a once great series to bed. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9975728410270501408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105664313?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780755352562" href="/book/show/7069295-bullet">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of erotica inc. m/m, m/m/f, f/f, BDSM</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=libricide">libricide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=i-heart-the-cover-art">i-heart-the-cover-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=do-not-own">do-not-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=menage-or-polyamory">menage-or-polyamory</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105664313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8784914431744777686"><i>
  <b>Stay away from it. Stay away. If you had any love for this series at any point, do not read this book. If you do, make sure you're a fan of erotica including m/m, m/m/f, f/f, and BDSM.</b>
</i><br/><br/>It’s shocking the abrupt u-turn the series takes with <i>Bullet</i>, deciding that sex (and lots of it) is better than guns, blood and action. The death of a character (not an important one so don’t worry) was anti-climactic, it was a good scene but I expected the death to be of someone a lot closer to Anita, and ther</span>
  <span id="freeText8784914431744777686" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Stay away from it. Stay away. If you had any love for this series at any point, do not read this book. If you do, make sure you're a fan of erotica including m/m, m/m/f, f/f, and BDSM.</b>
</i><br /><br />It’s shocking the abrupt u-turn the series takes with <i>Bullet</i>, deciding that sex (and lots of it) is better than guns, blood and action. The death of a character (not an important one so don’t worry) was anti-climactic, it was a good scene but I expected the death to be of someone a lot closer to Anita, and therefore more painful but she agonises over it anyway, despite knowing all along that they may have to die.<br /><br />Right off the bat we go into repetitive descriptive overload. Sex politics, self-pity and whining is in abundance. LKH even uses a three-year old boy in the first chapter to give us hope that Anita will rein in her loose ways, and then uses him again (at his expense, which offended me - children should be protected) at the end to stick two fingers up at those that dislike the porn. And I’m sad to say this did read like emotionless porn -the group sex with multiple voyeurs made me think "porn movie set" with everyone taking turns. And they were doing it to save lives or for political reasons rather than because they wanted it or because they loved each other. And since when was Anita OK with her men having sex with other women, or even Anita herself having sex with women? What?! Will the real Anita please stand up?<br /><br />Which leads me on to the main characters themselves who've have changed in ways I don't feel are realistic and the number of side characters has grown to a point where I don't remember who they are. Although LKH attempts to soothe my newfound dislike of Anita at the end of <i>Flirt</i> by making her remorseful. I can’t say it worked. She has become all-powerful and arrogant, a combination which is off-putting to put it mildly. Plus the reference to her and others possibly doing evil things in order to do good has put me on edge.<br /><br />All the bits that interested me, like the plot, shocking that there even was one but it was thin throughout. It was alluded to but there was little depth. Many references were made to previous books, characters reappear with Anita's relationships with them being reassessed however, big events happen elsewhere whilst we were stuck watching Anita have sex with everything that moved. I’m not exaggerating. I’m not even sure I have enough fingers to count out how many times she had sex, or even with the number of people. At least she wasn't the only one getting it this time. Although the m/m scene between Asher and Jean Claude was incredibly disappointing. They'd been pining for each other, desperate to re-consummate their love for so long, you'd think LKH could've taken the time to describe the emotional side of it better.<br /><br />More happened in the concluding chapter than in the entire book, which focused heavily on the tigers. I couldn't care less about them really, the info dump was boring. Given the chance I’d have wanted to witness the events (especially in Atlanta) in that chapter rather than the sex or sex politics. Instead they were glossed over. So sad.<br /><br />I dragged myself through this book, and employed everything possible to get to that last page. I skimmed, I skipped paragraphs/pages – there’s only so much repetitive description I could take. I can’t read another sex scene for a bit because I’ve had enough. Enough. Yep, that’s how I feel about this series now. Enough. I’m done.<br /><br />If I sound angry, bitter and wistful it’s because I’m all of those things. I’m angry that old-Anita is nowhere to be found despite her reappearance in the past couple of books. I’m bitter because I wasn’t expecting the abrupt change back to everything revolving around sex. I had hope and LKH had encouraged it, that old-Anita was resurfacing. She crushed it so forcefully that I don’t want anything more to do with her.<br /><br /><b>This series to me is now a sick and mangy wolf that needs to be put down, it's begging for an end to it's suffering. It needs a <i>Bullet</i> to the brain.</b></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-bad-it-s-good">so-bad-it-s-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=what-the-hell-did-i-just-read">what-the-hell-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=read-at-your-own-risk">read-at-your-own-risk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer891419640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12754239268083564698">Bullet Review:<br/><br/>(Get it?! BULLET Review? Of BULLET? Don't we have some BULLET inception going on here??)<br/><br/>Proof positive that LKH:<br/><br/>A) No longer gives a sh!t for her fans.<br/><br/>B) Is writing out her personal sexual fantasy.<br/><br/>C) Has absolutely no editor/editor needs to be tortured.<br/><br/>This is the biggest piece of sh!t since "Incubus Dreams" and "Danse Macabre". Pointless, plotless, meandering, with more scenes talking about everyone's feelings and sexual pairings (not necessarily sex, mind you!) than anything to d</span>
  <span id="freeText12754239268083564698" style="display:none">Bullet Review:<br><br>(Get it?! BULLET Review? Of BULLET? Don't we have some BULLET inception going on here??)<br><br>Proof positive that LKH:<br><br>A) No longer gives a sh!t for her fans.<br><br>B) Is writing out her personal sexual fantasy.<br><br>C) Has absolutely no editor/editor needs to be tortured.<br><br>This is the biggest piece of sh!t since "Incubus Dreams" and "Danse Macabre". Pointless, plotless, meandering, with more scenes talking about everyone's feelings and sexual pairings (not necessarily sex, mind you!) than anything to do with a "plot". Not sure at this point LKH even knows what a "plot" is - I'm pretty sure she thinks endless conversations with Anita asking "What does that mean?" and "Am I missing something?" constitute a plot.<br><br>Biggest entertainment value is from how ludicrous the writing is and how positively awful the book gets. A shame, because at one point a plot threatens to take over the book. Fortunately, LKH "saves" the book from having any merit by giving the most powerful necromancer in a hundred years the pitiful excuse that traveling is "too dangerous" and therefore she must stay locked up in the Circus of the Impotent - I mean, Damned.<br><br>If this can get published, ANYTHING can get published.<br><br>Full review:<br><br>"Funny how it's never your fault when you have to have sex with all these men, Anita." - Monica<br>"'I don't mean to be callous, but whatever you're feeling, get over it.' - Nicky<br><br>Cover Blurb:<br><br><blockquote>The triumvirate created by master vampire Jean-Claude, necromancer Anita Blake, and werewolf Richard Zeeman has made Jean-Claude one of the most powerful vampires in the U.S. -with the result that assassins are coming to St. Louis to kill them all.</blockquote><br><br>Whoever wrote this cover blurb needs a raise. <br><br>No, wait. Whoever wrote this cover blurb needs to take over the writing of these Anita Blake books.<br><br>Because honestly that cover blurb has more plot in one sentence than the ENTIRETY of "Bullet".<br><br>I take that back; there IS plot in this book. It is this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396626426i/9162220.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396626426i/9162221._SX540_.png" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and THIS:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396626426i/9162222._SY540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Just pretend that all these women have curly black hair and GINORMOUS boobs.</i><br><br>And when it is not any of those, it is HOURS UPON HOURS OF this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396626426i/9162223.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Only with 30 other men all in various states of undress. And a b!tchy, curly-haired woman who refers to her own breasts as "creamy goodness".<br><br><blockquote>"There was way too much yummy mounded goodness going on in front of me for me to be entirely comfortable meeting a roomful of strangers..."</blockquote><br><br>Don't believe me? I made a break-down of how much time was spent on these things for about the first half of the book and here's what I came up with:<br><br><blockquote>+ approx 1 hour spent at a dance recital for a kid who is not related to the Main Characters. Dance recital was for KIDS and focused more on Nathaniel and Jason. (And Stephen?)<br> <br>+ approx 1 hour spent with Asher arguing about his power and wanting to have sex.<br> <br>+ approx 45 min spent with Richard whinging about the dramaz he's endured since book 2. This is ALL RECAP for those of us who have read since the beginning.<br> <br>+ approx 45 min spent on an unsexy orgy with Anita (no surprise), Richard, Jean-Claude, and Asher. It has B-D-S-M, meaning the B-D-S-M that non-practitioners or baby practitioners think is super cool.<br> <br>+ approx 30 min spent with a pile of men including Richard, JC, Asher, Jason, Nathaniel, Micah, Crispin (who is this again?) and Nicky (the "bride" of Anita", because she poisoned him, isn't that CUTE?) on Anita. Belle Morte does that "appearing to everyone" bit and Marmee Noir makes a "I'm gonna keeeel you, MUAHAHAHAHAHA!" appearance.<br> <br>+ approx 45 min Anita recounting the events to Max, Viviana, and Augustine and asking "What does that mean?" over and over again. While she reclines on a bed, with a bunch of naked men covered in lion goop.<br> <br>+ approx 30 min of Anita facing off Haven (may I add, this is just in the living room of the Circus of the Damned, mere yards from an earlier black-out orgy - one, might I add that was non-consensual, but that EVERYONE wishes they could have been there)<br> <br>+ approx 30 min of Anita talking about the post-black-out orgy that Marmee Noir did for EVULZ reasons (while they are all nude and covered in goop)<br> <br>+ approx 30 min of Anita arguing with Haven (wherein he whines about her not "loving him" and wanting him as her Rex)</blockquote><br><br>So, uh...where's the EVUL assassins the cover blurb promised? How are Anita and Richard and Jean-Claude getting so uber powerful?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396626426i/9162224._SX540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh right...I'm just a prudey prude who doesn't like sex. It's not like I'm a reader who maybe kinda was expecting, oh, I don't know, a STORY, a PLOT in this book. Nope, prudey prude. Gotcha.<br><br>I started reading these books about two years ago because everyone talked about how awesome they were, how gritty, how they were like the best Urban Fantasy out there (with the caveat "up until Obsidian Butterfly"). I was never a fan of Anita because I thought she was a horrible woman who acted like a child and never grew up - but damn if that Anita wasn't a Saint compared to this one.<br><br>At least she didn't ask "What does that mean?" or "Am I missing something?" EVER OTHER PARAGRAPH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349887ra/703798.gif" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously, woman, you've been in this field for 4+ years, and you've been doing the horizontal tango with paranormals since like book 4. YOU SHOULD KNOW THIS ALREADY.<br><br>But no, Anita Blake hasn't grown one twit since Book 1. She's still the same angry, violent, clueless woman. She still has hangups about having sex, which is weird given she's been having sex for more books than she was not. And, in her defense, I don't care for how often she HAS to have sex or HAS to add a new partner. But beyond that - shouldn't she be used to this thing by now?<br><br>I guess I could talk about the other 50 billion men that are in this book. Oh and three women. Because Anita's world is almost 100% male. I'm not even joking; I canNOT even attempt to write all the male names that I came across. Beyond Micah, Nathaniel, JC, Richard, Asher, Damien, Jason, and Haven, there were loads and loads and loads more. Guards, potential sex partners, Masters of the City. Sure, a couple of token women like Claudia and Cardinal and Viviana were thrown in. But when you can count the women on two hands and the men outnumber them 30:1, you have a problem.<br><br>And these men! Good God, LKH can spend 80 paragraphs on their clothes:<br><br><blockquote>"Jean-Claude's black leather pants looked poured on, and his boots rose up over his thighs like a second skin. I didn't have to see the back of his boots to see they laced all the way up his leg."</blockquote><br><i>In short, he looks like a fisherman going out to wade.</i><br><br>and the special shade of green their eyes are:<br><br><blockquote>"I gazed up into those midnight blue eyes so dark that a few shades darker and the blue would have been lost to a black. But they were forever the blue of the sky just as the light begins to leave but darkness is still a few breaths away."</blockquote><br><i>Sorry, blue.</i><br><br>But I still couldn't tell them apart in a lineup. Other than their One Defining CharacteristicTM:<br><br>Jean-Claude: Calls Anita "Ma Petit"<br>Richard: Manly man<br>Micah: Kitty-cat eyes<br>Nathaniel: Ankle-length hair<br>Asher: Most beautiful angsty bisexual EVAH<br>Jason: Anita's sometime lover<br>Damien: GREEN eyes, greener than anything that was ever green<br><br>And that's all there is to these characters now. In the course of this book, two characters die (leading Anita to spend hours upon hours wangsting over their deaths), but I honestly barely remembered one and didn't give two sh!ts that the other one died. I was actually grateful as he was one of her boytoys - until she went and acquired a new one. Named Mephistopheles.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396365644ra/9123040.gif" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dear Ms. Hamilton: STOP USING STUPID NAMES FOR YOUR CHARACTERS. You are in your 40's, not some emo, angsty teenager writing out her wet dreams.<br><br>Or maybe...<br><br>I really could go on and on about all the individual stupid things in this book. The latent misogyny and sexism (once again, ALL WOMEN buy the latest fashions and dresses and can't believe it when you don't!). The inability to understand what makes a person gay or bisexual (and no, it's not because they were abused by the opposite sex and are "taking a break"). How everyone has sex for every reason EXCEPT for how they want to get lucky. How the word spill has been violently abused to describe everything EXCEPT LIQUIDS.<br><br><blockquote>""All my scrambling in the pillows during the orgasm had spilled me to one side of the mounded pillows, so that they hid the other two men."</blockquote><br><br>But now I want to rag on the writing. Because people...THIS GOT PUBLISHED. UNDER A BIG NAME. AND PEOPLE BOUGHT IT HARDCOVER PRICE. And at the risk of losing my credibility, this isn't like EL James or the many push-to-publish authors who wrote fanfiction and brushed it up a bit for self-publish or even big name. They HAVE excuses for having juvenile, choppy, bad prose. But LKH should know better; this is her more than her 19th book!<br><br>Top 5 LKH Quotes That Make You Question Life, the Universe, Everything<br><br>1. "I felt myself smile, and it wasn't a nice smile." It was a not nice smile. A smile that would smile it's way into your heart, smile and then smile as it smiled at you.<br><br>2. "It tasted good enough that I knew I was a lot hungrier than I knew." I also knew that this book would be worse than I knew.<br><br>3. "If I craved it and gave into it, I would be the monster. I didn't want to be the monster...was that monstrous? ...the only difference between being the monster and being powerful was choosing not to be the monster. Not today. But there would always be tomorrow and another chance to choose." Ah, Anita Blake, Philosopher. Actually, given how this series has devolved from Vampire Hunter to Vampire Humper, that would be an improvement.<br><br>4. "We'd discovered that if you left the drink in the screwtop cups that helped stirred them up, you never really got the cups clean. The remains of the protein powder solidified in the cracks and crevices, and you just had to throw out the cup." Because it's more important that a VAMPIRE HUNTER novel talk about how to clean the crap out of a protein shake cup than about killing Vampires.<br><br>5. "Tell me you don't want him, and this stops here. But if you want him the way I felt you want him, then don't lie to yourself or to him. Want him or don't want him, but if you want him, let yourself want him." <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396627523i/9162406.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What "progress" "Skin Trade", "The Harlequin" and even "Flirt" made to "bring Anita back" is completely gone here. And the sad thing is, it didn't have to be this way. At one point, Anita gets a call to consult, and the story thread is just as good as anything in the earlier books. The only problem is that Anita chickens out of going to Atlanta to DO SOMETHING, saying it's "too dangerous" for the most powerful necromancer and 80 of her guards to leave and, I dunno, hunt some vampires.<br><br>These books are the bottom of the barrel, the only entertainment value being in noting how many times the word "spill" is used and, my favorite, Anita Blake Bingo. And yes, I did win, even if it took me to the very end of the book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1396627486p8/967747.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12754239268083564698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_110251036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110251036" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110251036?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">My worst enemy, perhaps. Might be too cruel.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=glutton_for_punishment">glutton_for_punishment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2010">vanquished_2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110251036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3185531060264242050">If my updates weren’t expressive enough, I’ll reiterate: This is the most tedious drivel I’ve read in a long time…or perhaps ever.<br/><br/>Although the idea of a vampire civil war should be a thrilling one, LKH’s writing deprives it of all excitement. The events of this book seem like a rehash of every other attack we’ve seen on the supernatural sect of St. Louis. If you’re a long-time reader of the series, very little will seem new.<br/><br/>I could easily blather on about the lack of innovation present in Bullet</span>
  <span id="freeText3185531060264242050" style="display:none">If my updates weren’t expressive enough, I’ll reiterate: This is the most tedious drivel I’ve read in a long time…or perhaps ever.<br /><br />Although the idea of a vampire civil war should be a thrilling one, LKH’s writing deprives it of all excitement. The events of this book seem like a rehash of every other attack we’ve seen on the supernatural sect of St. Louis. If you’re a long-time reader of the series, very little will seem new.<br /><br />I could easily blather on about the lack of innovation present in Bullet, but instead I’ll focus on a few irksome aspects. Although I’ve never envisioned Anita as a startling intellect, the dialogue here paints her as an absolute mental midget. Pages and pages of various men explaining simple concepts to her and Anita continuously parroting: “But why?” “What does that mean?” “What does he mean by that?” “What am I missing?” Apparently, my dear, you are missing a vast amount of brain power. And when she finally grasps the idea presented, her only response is: “I don’t know what to say to that.”<br /><br />The basics of this exchange are repeated every few pages, making most conversations feel like pulling teeth and inspiring me to smack my forehead no less than twenty times. If Anita is this thick, I can’t imagine how she’s managed to live this long, never mind build her power center up to unfathomable proportions.<br /><br />Hand-in-hand with Anita’s stupidity is her inability to be reasonable. Constantly on the defensive, she forces all of her men to tiptoe around her in trepidation. And yet! She feels immeasurable guilt about having taken away Nicky’s free will. Guess what, dumb-dumb. With every one around you in fear of getting dumped--or perhaps shot--absolutely no one in the group can exercise free will. They are <i>all</i> slaves of some sort to the sorcerous snatch. <br /><br />Speaking of that wondrous body part, I’ve heard time and again that this series is as much about Anita’s “sexual awakening” as it is about vampires and weres, oh my. Though I grant that she’s come a long way from the virginal prude of Guilty Pleasures, Anita has not been awakened. She has been coerced, cajoled, convinced, and given the excuses she needs to allow herself--after much waffling--to fall into bed with various people. Even in this book, she spends more time trying to get out of having sex than she does actively wanting it. It is only when someone badgers her into responding to her “monstrous” side that she willingly goes along with physical intimacy. More often than not, she is embarrassed by her sexual desires. That does not scream “awakening” to me. <br /><br />I’d already decided when I read Flirt that I would no longer throw money into LKH’s coffers. Having gotten Bullet from the library, I think even that small nod of encouragement was wasted on her. The quality of writing is beneath that of any writer I’m familiar with. Her plots have become secondary to descriptions of wardrobe, hair, and seating plans. Sex scenes are robbed of eroticism. Dialogue brings the action to a screeching, painful halt. I no longer find anything of merit in the Anita Blake series, so I bid these characters a not-so-fond adieu. Don’t let the door smack you on the way out.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3185531060264242050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83256280?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mlady_rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mlady_rebecca" href="/user/show/732709-mlady-rebecca">mlady_rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=characters__lycanthropes_shifters">characters__lycanthropes_shifters</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=fiction__speculative">fiction__speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=series__anita_blake">series__anita_blake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=author__laurell_k_hamilton__ab">author__laurell_k_hamilton__ab</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=characters__vamps">characters__vamps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=genre__urban_fantasy">genre__urban_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=read_more_than_once">read_more_than_once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732709-mlady-rebecca?shelf=abvh__us_hb_v2__horror">abvh__us_hb_v2__horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83256280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer705685237303267589">"Bullet" was all the good things I like to see in an "Anita Blake" book, and some.<br/><br/>1. It was home in St. Louis, because - aside from "Bloody Bones", "Blue Moon", and "Blood Noir" (all "B" names - weird) - all of the out of town books seem to be lacking something. <br/><br/>2. It included the fullest cast list we've seen since (at least) "The Harlequin". And most of those cast members had more than a walk on role.<br/><br/>3. It was heavy on vampire and furry politics, and light on federal marshal duties.<br/><br/>4. The littl</span>
  <span id="freeText705685237303267589" style="display:none">"Bullet" was all the good things I like to see in an "Anita Blake" book, and some.<br /><br />1. It was home in St. Louis, because - aside from "Bloody Bones", "Blue Moon", and "Blood Noir" (all "B" names - weird) - all of the out of town books seem to be lacking something. <br /><br />2. It included the fullest cast list we've seen since (at least) "The Harlequin". And most of those cast members had more than a walk on role.<br /><br />3. It was heavy on vampire and furry politics, and light on federal marshal duties.<br /><br />4. The little we saw of federal marshal duties, showed that Anita continues to embrace the role of advocate over the role of executioner. (Off stage, we find out she supported legislation that if a Master of the City went crazy and had to be assassinated, the remaining Masters were to be given a chance.)<br /><br />5. It tied up a hell of a lot of loose threads. Some of which were painfully obvious - like Haven and the fate of the Mother of all Darkness - and some of which you didn't even realize had been hanging.<br /><br />6. The sex was heavier on the side of Anita's sweeties, as opposed to strangers.<br /><br />7. There was a resolution of sorts with respect to some of the moodier guys in Anita's life - Asher, Richard, and Haven.<br /><br />8. We got more information on the Vampire Council and the various lines. Which I personally find fascinating. <br /><br />9. There is progress in the consolidation of power among Anita's two triumverates.<br /><br />10. Most of the extra guys Anita has bonded with - like Crispen, Domino, and Nicky - have fallen into a close but not too close role. They aren't constantly demanding more, like say Requiem, who apparently did move out of town, although he's never mentioned explicitly. <br /><br />I think that covers everything I can say without dipping into spoilers. A spoiler rich review may follow. <br /><br />Can't recommend enough. *g*</span>
  <a data-text-id="705685237303267589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorena" href="/user/show/251417-lorena">Lorena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251417-lorena?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251417-lorena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106133655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14025384381366108012">Recommended only for those whose doctors have prescribed a daily session of eye-rolling to increase eye mobility. There really isn't anything to say about this book, because nothing really happens. All semblance of plotting has been entirely overthrown so that Laurell - whoops, I mean "Anita" - can think about and talk about and have group sex for pretty much the entire book. And even that would have value as titillation if there were more "having" than "thinking about and talking about." But th</span>
  <span id="freeText14025384381366108012" style="display:none">Recommended only for those whose doctors have prescribed a daily session of eye-rolling to increase eye mobility. There really isn't anything to say about this book, because nothing really happens. All semblance of plotting has been entirely overthrown so that Laurell - whoops, I mean "Anita" - can think about and talk about and have group sex for pretty much the entire book. And even that would have value as titillation if there were more "having" than "thinking about and talking about." But there is not. It's like hanging out with that friend who just got into therapy, and thinks everyone else is as fascinated as she is with examining every detail of her life under a microscope, or that guy who just found religion and now works it into every conversation, trying to convert you. In other words, tiresome. Repetitive. Nowhere near as clever/deep as it thinks it is. Constantly presenting stuff most people figured out years ago as new, shocking, and original. If there IS one thing to say about this book it would be "God, shut UP, Anita." Repeat at least once per page. And roll your eyes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14025384381366108012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104479761" />
    <a title="Mandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2987532-mandi"><img alt="Mandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424479076p2/2987532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104479761?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandi" href="/user/show/2987532-mandi">Mandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2987532-mandi?shelf=paranormal-urban-romance">paranormal-urban-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2987532-mandi?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104479761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12805901605264096974">Wow.<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9550.Laurell_K__Hamilton' title='Laurell K. Hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laurell K. Hamilton</a> came back swinging hard with this book. A book that's finally set in St. Louis with all of our favourites. Jean-Claude, Asher, Nathaniel, Micah, Jason and Richard! Yup even Richard and like LKH mentioned he is back to his old self. The therapist he's seen really did something great for him. He's there for the triumvirate and he's even more swoonish then he was. I can totally understand why Laurell and Anita would both be so hesitant to trust him again. Every page is thril</span>
  <span id="freeText12805901605264096974" style="display:none">Wow.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9550.Laurell_K__Hamilton" title="Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Laurell K. Hamilton</a> came back swinging hard with this book. A book that's finally set in St. Louis with all of our favourites. Jean-Claude, Asher, Nathaniel, Micah, Jason and Richard! Yup even Richard and like LKH mentioned he is back to his old self. The therapist he's seen really did something great for him. He's there for the triumvirate and he's even more swoonish then he was. I can totally understand why Laurell and Anita would both be so hesitant to trust him again. Every page is thrilling, every word eggs you to keep reading, even if it's nearly 3 am and you have to work early in the morning. The novel is so totally worth being sleep deprived. <br /><br />It was entertaining to watch <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9550.Laurell_K__Hamilton" title="Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Laurell K. Hamilton</a> tweet about the books and the death that she mentioned, it was epic. Someone who you least expected to die, died and in a shocking way. After reading that scene i understand why it was so hard to get back. The scene after is heart-breaking numbing and it might take a few reads to full understand the magnitude of just how much that person meant to Anita. With the Marmee Noir on her back it's also adds a twist to it all.<br /><br />All in all this book really was a great read and it was worth waiting two books to get to where Anita is now. It was also great to see Anita further her knowledge about her powers and just what she can do. Definitely worth the wait. Amazing Laurell!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12805901605264096974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104223388?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wicked Lil Pixie (Natasha)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wicked Lil Pixie (Natasha)" href="/user/show/2863148-wicked-lil-pixie-natasha">Wicked Lil Pixie (Natasha)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104223388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6182570658891072922">The main storyline surrounds Anita, the triumvirate, her animals to call & an unexpected reunion with the Mother of All Darkness who everyone thought was dead. Because of the return of the Mother of All Darkness, Anita must come to terms with all the men surrounding her & try to complete the cats she calls. On top of it, Richard comes back & Anita doesn’t know if she can trust him again. Then we have an appearance by Haven & he is demanding Anita’s love, it’s all or nothing for Haven.<br/><br/>For you Ani</span>
  <span id="freeText6182570658891072922" style="display:none">The main storyline surrounds Anita, the triumvirate, her animals to call &amp; an unexpected reunion with the Mother of All Darkness who everyone thought was dead. Because of the return of the Mother of All Darkness, Anita must come to terms with all the men surrounding her &amp; try to complete the cats she calls. On top of it, Richard comes back &amp; Anita doesn’t know if she can trust him again. Then we have an appearance by Haven &amp; he is demanding Anita’s love, it’s all or nothing for Haven.<br /><br />For you Anita fans, there is lots of Jean-Claude, Asher, Nathaniel &amp; Richard time! Let me tell you, Richard really grows up in this book &amp; Asher is still my absolute favorite. Micah is around but not as prominent as in other books in the series. There are new females introduced, which we haven’t really seen before in an Anita book, so we get to see how Anita interacts with new females. It also has a really dark &amp; disturbing moment with child vampire Valentina, which totally creeped me out. She has to be the scariest vampire in any book I’ve read, children always scare me worse than anything but Valentina is just horrid.<br /><br />Of course it wouldn’t be an Anita book without some hot romance scenes, I kid you not LKH is the only author that makes me squirm when I read her sex scenes. It got all sorts of hot at some points! *grabs a cold cloth*<br /><br />What I found with Bullet was that it ties up a lot of loose information, from Asher &amp; Jean-Claude to Richard and his issues. It’s closure for the old drama &amp; setting up for a huge battle(s) in book 20 of the series. It also is a book of growth for Anita, she goes through some very bad experiences &amp; has to either move on with her life or just breakdown. There’s completion &amp; new openings, so you know book 20 is going to be something huge!<br /><br />Thankfully Laurell K. Hamilton is currently writing book 20 in the series, so the wait isn’t going to be too long! Long time fans of the series will like Bullet, but book 20 is the one we’ll all be waiting for.</span>

<div id="review_110558857" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110558857" />
    <a title="Kevin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2240181-kevin"><img alt="Kevin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374702578p2/2240181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110558857?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin" href="/user/show/2240181-kevin">Kevin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110558857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11492542883802183590">First, beyond anything else, Ms. Hamilton needs an editor. Tortured prose, dangling plot threads, indeterminate pronouns, etc.<br/><br/>**SPOILERS**<br/><br/>So, the big Mother of All Night comes back, everyone worries about it, f**ks about it, TALKS about it for several HUNDRED pages, and what it really comes down to is Anita screwing a few tigers of a different color at one of those dreary vampire cocktail parties with all the boots and bare chests, and complete and utter lack of anything remotely resembling pers</span>
  <span id="freeText11492542883802183590" style="display:none">First, beyond anything else, Ms. Hamilton needs an editor. Tortured prose, dangling plot threads, indeterminate pronouns, etc.<br /><br />**SPOILERS**<br /><br />So, the big Mother of All Night comes back, everyone worries about it, f**ks about it, TALKS about it for several HUNDRED pages, and what it really comes down to is Anita screwing a few tigers of a different color at one of those dreary vampire cocktail parties with all the boots and bare chests, and complete and utter lack of anything remotely resembling personal boundaries, or even personality, and that's it. Mamma Darkness on the run, the Harlequin appeased, and the American Masters roll over, the end. (Wait: Baby Matthew. Awwwww. Or, more accurately, Ewwww. Let us avoid discussing Baby Matt's disturbing precocity, shall we?)<br /><br />Anita has the most deadly amazing vajayjay since "Liquid Sky." She doesn't even have to get out of bed to destroy evil, since the power of her lady parts draws all who would fight the powers of darkness directly to her. We never even see any more of St. Louis than the inside of her bedrooms anymore. All of the action, such as it is, takes place en suite.<br /><br />Ms. Hamilton isn't even trying to throw the thinnest of veils across the fact that ALL of her characters are simply extensions of Anita's Omnipotent Punani. Notice how no one actually does anything of any note outside of Anita's immediate vicinity, usually with skin-to-skin contact. Are the other vamps and weres powerful? I dunno. I hear that they are, but all they ever do is feed Anita's powers. {Jan Brady voice: "Anita! Anita! Anita!} That scene where literally EVERYone ended up in her bed fighting off Belle and Padma was a perfect representation of what the entire series has become: Anita and the Preternatural Pseudopods. The only character that acts with any personal autonomy (Haven, who IS a bastard) gets his brains blown out, and poor Richard nearly buys it for daring to step outside the Circus for 10 minutes for a lousy date (fortunately, he is rescued by the Amazing Voracious Supersnatch, long distance). It appears that we are working through some serious abandonment issues here, which, alas, is boring.<br /><br />Also, I'm freaking sick to death of all the hairography. I wonder if she has actually seen anyone with hair "down to their ankles?" It ain't pretty. In fact, it's actually kinda gross. Remember Crystal Gale? She used to sit on her hair when she appeared on chat shows, which was definitely a thing that made me go, "Ick." I suppose that all her weres and vamps (like Merry's Fairies) have preternatural powers of shine, body and bounce, because otherwise, that shit is naAASty.<br /><br />This was the last one for me, at last. I entertained some small hope after "Skin Trade," but "Flirt" and "Bullet" have mercilessly quashed that hope. Hope that once sang and surged through my veins, rising, cresting with the taste of blood and musk, quivering on the tips of my turgid, tumescent taste buds, awaiting just the barest trace of the scent of a plot to fulfill it, to fulfil me, as that taste of hope burst from my tongue as husky, duskily glorious song, only to be extinguished by the soul- and tongue-withering disappointment of an empty story, sadly lost and never found. Only cerements and ashes. Ashes and hair lay dead upon my dry, distended, thrice-bitten unhappy toungue.<br /><br />I'm out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11492542883802183590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11075223847736872356">Don't let Skin Trade fool ya folks! LKH didn't seem to actually realize that there was too much f...ahem, fluff, and not enough (non sexual) action.<br/><br/>My favourite books are the Edward ones, followed by the original Wereanimal ones. So that pretty much sums up how i feel about them swanning around the circus not doing much (except each other).<br/><br/>After Anita killed someone and spent a good chapter angst it out, i thought she would jump on the chance to get out there, be a big bad Marshall and go take d</span>
  <span id="freeText11075223847736872356" style="display:none">Don't let Skin Trade fool ya folks! LKH didn't seem to actually realize that there was too much f...ahem, fluff, and not enough (non sexual) action.<br /><br />My favourite books are the Edward ones, followed by the original Wereanimal ones. So that pretty much sums up how i feel about them swanning around the circus not doing much (except each other).<br /><br />After Anita killed someone and spent a good chapter angst it out, i thought she would jump on the chance to get out there, be a big bad Marshall and go take down the rotter in Atlanta. When she was sent the video/ Surely that seals the deal, so kick some vampire but! <br /><br />But no, she had a party to attend with some weretigers! *facedesk* I don't care how good a party it was, our Anita is gone. She has been totally rolled.<br /><br />Also, i am sick to the back teeth of "poured on" and "painted on" leather. Now, I'm as partial to the idea of beautiful sexually ambiguous men in leather as the next woman, but jesus christ you really do not need to write a new costume for each character every scene, especially when they always wear the same sort of thing. You end up with drivel like "He was wearing leather that looked poured on with knee high boots...I liked him when he wore nothing but the knee high leather boots...even without the knee high leather boots those painted on leather trousers..." blah blah. We get it. JC wears leather, and likes everyone else to as well. So they do at his house and his parties. The End.<br /><br />I am also very over Asher. I was actually excited when he threatened to leave. Get your whiney attitude and leave. Just don't take Narcissus because he is super interesting, and if LKH ever writes something with him in again we may be saved.<br /><br />It feels like even the sex in these books has devolved into ego stroking. If you have like, 20 million plus men (and now apparently, women) waiting to sleep with you, and you are in love with a good what, 5+ of them? If someone needs 5 pages of being told they are beautiful and reassurance that you want to sleep with them, they ain't worth it!<br /><br />I also didn't like that anything interesting that DID happen actually happened off page. Richards big emotional U Turn for one. Um, hello! Where did you come from? Others were brushed away with barely a sentence - "Oh yeah, Richard had to hunt and kill some guys and he cried so that's cool now". Sorry, but that's the stuff i DO want.<br /><br />The only other scene that disappointed me was when all the females squared off against Haven. Finally, i thought Anita would have some female friends, some female perspective. No, that was brushed away pretty fast.<br /><br />It was entertaining enough in its own smutty way, but seriously LKH, get her away from the boys. Get her out there being a Marshall.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4492541376957186268"><b>Good things:</b><br/><br/>* Richard (the most annoying man on the planet and in a world with Asher that says something) quit being so angry and whiny. But LKH never delved into why. In a book that details how to wash out a cup after drinking a protein shake, you'd think something this big would get some ink.<br/><br/>* The video from the rotter massacre in Atlanta was actually interesting. Too bad all the resolution happened off screen while we got to read about Anita's wardrobe.<br/><br/>* JC was actually <b>in</b> this book. He was c</span>
  <span id="freeText4492541376957186268" style="display:none"><b>Good things:</b><br /><br />* Richard (the most annoying man on the planet and in a world with Asher that says something) quit being so angry and whiny. But LKH never delved into why. In a book that details how to wash out a cup after drinking a protein shake, you'd think something this big would get some ink.<br /><br />* The video from the rotter massacre in Atlanta was actually interesting. Too bad all the resolution happened off screen while we got to read about Anita's wardrobe.<br /><br />* JC was actually <b>in</b> this book. He was completely whipped and a shell of the man a lot of us fans fell hard for, but he was present.<br /><br /><b>The Rest:</b><br /><br />What can I say... no Edward, barely any plot, another woke up looked at all the naked people and didn't know what happened scene, no London ... *sigh*.<br /><br />I really want executioner-animator Anita to be the MC of a book; not some whiny, self-obsessed, not-kicking-ass girl who spends too much time thinking about her breasts "yummy mounded goodness" *groan* and employing her magical vagina as often as possible.<br /><br />I'm not a prude and I was a huge fan of the first books. This was just so plot-thin by comparison.<br /><br />The thing I hated most was all the "showing" LKH wrote went to the sex and the talking about feelings but for the plot she used "telling" and ruined the little bit there was. A few pages away from the end of the book I was excitedly thinking, Wow! how are they going to pull this out of the fire? Something very big must happen (or maybe this is just a set-up for the next book). Nope. Instead we got what amounted to a shy two pages of,<br /><br />Jake hunted Padma!<br /><br />Richard killed his attackers and cried!<br /><br />(You know what would have been awesome? If Edward showed up with his bags of destruction and he and Anita take off on an around the world man-hunt. That's a book I'd be marking my calendar to read the next installment of.)<br /><br />The writing was beyond repetitive, both of this book and the ones that came before, and it had cheap amateur scenes like the opening chapter at the dance where they describe each person. Ugh. (As an aside, who has multi-age dance recitals with two year olds and wereanimal strippers in a school?).<br /><br />Someone please take away all sharp objects if I ever have to read any variation of "poured into painted on leather pants", "wet but tight", "couldn't make sense of it because your mind wants to spare you from what your eyes are seeing" etc. ever again.<br /><br />Why do I keep reading? <br /><br />I love the world and I love who the characters used to be. <br /><br />This book was just another in a long list of Anita Blake novels that sully a good thing and turn characters into cardboard.</span>

  <span id="freeText7497530175422399058" style="display:none">Crash...and....burn.<br /><br />R.I.P. awesome kick butt Anita that I fell in love with all those years ago. <br /><br />I remember a day when the thought of no more AB books made me VERY sad. I devoured them often in one night, and waited in anticipation for the next book. Now I can honestly say I'd rather have had LHK stop 6-7 books ago and end the series abruptly then have it come to this...this....thing it has become.<br /><br />I have continued to read the series (if you want to call it read, it's more of a skim) over the last few years because I really did fall in love with a few of the characters. I wish to God that I hadn't read this book however, because in it is the complete destruction of everything that made this series so great. I may be overly dramatic, but honestly, LKH, you had a good thing going and you just ruined it. I have no doubt that you can be a talented writer, there is proof of that in the page turners you once dished out. But for the sake of all that was good about this series, just end it, please? PLEASE?<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7497530175422399058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16993989132094685643" style="display:none"><br />Up to and including Obsidian Butterfly, the Anita Blake series was hands down one of the best series I've ever read. Since then, however, this series is just one big disappointment....yet I keep reading them, hoping, wishing, that one day Laurell K. Hamilton will bring the real Anita back.<br /><br />Bullet was, well, ridiculous. Whine, whine, whine about killing someone (ummm...Anita kills for a living). Talk and/or think everything (and nothing) to death. No action (unless in the bedroom, of course, which at this point has become tedious to read).<br /><br />On page 356 of 356 the book says "I'm a U.S. Marshal, a legal vampire executioner, and I raise the dead for a living." Dead men's penises maybe. <br /><br />These books have become self indulgent on the author's part. I think LKH sees herself as Anita, bringing in her own BDSM fetishes and leaving Anita out of the books entirely. Huge thumbs down. I may borrow future installments, but I won't be spending anymore money on her books.</span>

<div id="review_105485411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105485411" />
    <a title="Lindsey Simard Toutant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3265473-lindsey-simard-toutant"><img alt="Lindsey Simard Toutant" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272926858p2/3265473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105485411?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey Simard Toutant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey Simard Toutant" href="/user/show/3265473-lindsey-simard-toutant">Lindsey Simard Toutant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105485411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3805185888603779907">*Warning: This novel has a high volume of sexual content and this novel and my review may not be appropriate for young readers. Read at your own risk!* <br/><br/><br/>Before I get to my review I would like a moment to gush and tell you that throughout this novel I had to repeatedly put this novel down and fan myself before I spontaniously combusted. When I finished the novel and my husband asked what I though about it I was momentarily speechless. This novel is very, very naughty and very, very, very delicious</span>
  <span id="freeText3805185888603779907" style="display:none">*Warning: This novel has a high volume of sexual content and this novel and my review may not be appropriate for young readers. Read at your own risk!* <br /><br /><br />Before I get to my review I would like a moment to gush and tell you that throughout this novel I had to repeatedly put this novel down and fan myself before I spontaniously combusted. When I finished the novel and my husband asked what I though about it I was momentarily speechless. This novel is very, very naughty and very, very, very delicious....<br /><br /><br />Onto my review!<br /><br /><br />I have had the pleasure of reading the Anita Blake Vampire Hunter Series for more years then I can remember and she is one of the few authors who's characters have become like old friends. Some protagonists I am able to identify with because I see myself in them but I don't see myself in Anita; for me that is what is so thrilling about her as a character. While reading an Anita Blake novel you can escape to another exciting world where all the dark desires you have and those you didn't even know you have can be explored.<br /><br /><br />In the beginning of the series there was more of a focus on Anita as a necromancer, the solving of a paranormal crime, and the development of her romantic life. As many readers of Hamilton know, throughout the series the level of sexual content has increased dramatically which has had mixed reviews. At times I have felt that the sexual content has overshadowed the main plot of her novels but despite this I am never disappointed because Hamilton writes erotic sex scenes better then anyone else I have ever read. <br /><br /><br />The newest addition to this Anita Blake Series, Bullet had the best balance of sexual content and paranormal plot lines that I have read in this series to date. Readers be aware that Hamilton takes Anita's sexcapades to a whole new level of eroticism. While reading the sex scenes in this novel I felt like a naughty voyeur and many times I felt myself blushing. Much of the reason for this progression seems to be because Anita has become more accepting and comfortable with the Ardeur, the men her life, and her own needs. The level of sexual content is also necessary because Anita gains power for herself and her people through sex and with the unexpected return of The Mother Of All Darkness Anita, her loved ones, and the entire population of humans and paranormal people alike will need Anita and those she is connected with to be at their most powerful if they have any hope of defeating her.<br /><br /><br />This book also delves back into the history of vampire and shifter lore and further explores the politics of the paranormal world Anita lives in. The characters I have come to love are spotlighted well throughout the novel and an old romantic love of Anita's that I had all but written off makes a surprising comeback. New characters are introduced that I was at first apprehensive about but surprisingly I feel that they help to complete an already large family unit and I can't wait to see their characters develop in future books. <br /><br /><br />This book was tantalizing, suspenseful, erotic, and very well written. Hamilton's ability to describe scenes in such vivid detail allow me to see into her world better then any other author I have ever read in the paranormal urban fantasy genre. This novel exceeded my expectations by engaging me from beginning to end and I expect that future novels in this series will do the same.<br /><br /><br />If ever we create a personalized virtual reality system I know the first place I am going to visit ;) Hello Nethaniel, Jason, Jean-Claude, Asher, and Micah...which way to the bedroom?<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3805185888603779907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
